# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Grafana backend plugin management system and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I've identified all Go source files implementing Grafana's backend plugin management, which consists of:

**1. Process Supervisor** (`pkg/plugins/manager/process/process.go`)
- The `Service` struct manages plugin lifecycle with Start/Stop methods
- Core restart policy: `keepPluginAlive` function continuously monitors plugin processes and automatically restarts crashed plugins using a 1-second ticker

**2. gRPC Client Connection** (Multiple files in `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/`)
- `grpc_plugin.go`: Core gRPC plugin implementation using hashicorp/go-plugin with protocol negotiation
- `client.go`: Factory functions and gRPC client configuration (process/container modes)
- `client_v2.go`: Aggregated gRPC service clients (Diagnostics, Resource, Data, Stream, etc.)
- `client_proto.go`: High-level ProtoClient interface wrapping internal implementation

**3. Health Checks**
- Integrated through `CheckHealth` methods in both `grpcPlugin` and `ClientV2`
- Handles plugin unavailability gracefully

**4. Crash Recovery Policy**
- Automatic detection via `p.Exited()` polling
- Restarts only non-core plugins that crash
- Graceful error handling with retry attempts
- Stops on decommissioning

**5. Initialization & Termination Pipeline**
- `BackendClientInit`: Registers backend clients
- `BackendClientStarter`: Starts processes via manager
- `BackendProcessTerminator`: Cleanly stops processes
- `Deregister`: Removes from registry post-termination

The answer file includes detailed cross-references with symbols, call chains, and a comprehensive narrative explaining the complete architecture.

The `Service` struct (ProvideService) manages the complete lifecycle of backend plugins:\\n\\n- **Start method**: Initiates plugin processes for managed backend plugins and launches automatic crash recovery via `startPluginAndKeepItAlive`\\n- **keepPluginAlive function**: Implements the restart policy by continuously monitoring plugin processes using a ticker (default 1-second intervals). `p.Decommission()` and `p.Stop(ctx)`\\n\\nThe `Manager` interface in `pkg/plugins/manager/process/ifaces.go` defines the contract with Start and Stop methods.\\n\\n## gRPC Client Connection\\n\\ngRPC `grpcPlugin` for external consumption\\n- Methods like QueryData, CallResource, CheckHealth delegate to underlying ClientV2 implementations\\n\\n## Health Check Implementation\\n\\nHealth checking is the actual gRPC health check call to the plugin's DiagnosticsClient\\n  - Handles Unimplemented status gracefully (returns HealthStatusUnknown)\\n  - Converts between backend.CheckHealthRequest and pluginv2 protobuf messages\\n  - Returns error if plugin client is unavailable\\n\\n## Plugin Restart Policy on Crash\\n\\nThe crash recovery system is sophisticated:\\n\\n1. **Automatic Detection**: `keepPluginAlive` continuously polls via ticker, detecting crashed processes through `p.Exited()`\\n2. **Non-Core Plugin Only**: Core plugins are excluded from restart monitoring (checked in `startPluginAndKeepItAlive`)\\n3. **Graceful Restart**: On crash detection, the system logs the event and attempts restart via `p.Start(context.Background())`\\n4. **Error Handling**: If restart fails, the error is logged but the monitoring continues trying in future ticks\\n5. **Graceful Shutdown**: Decommissioned plugins are detected and monitoring stops automatically\\n\\n## Initialization `Deregister.Deregister`: Removes plugins from the registry after termination\\n\\nThe backend plugin system in Grafana provides resilient, self-healing plugin process management with automatic crash recovery, gRPC-based inter-process communication, and integrated health checking.\"\n}\n",

management is implemented through a multi-layered architecture combining process supervision, gRPC client communication, health checking, and automatic crash recovery.\\n\\n## Process Supervisor and Lifecycle Management\\n\\nThe core process supervisor is implemented in `pkg/plugins/manager/process/process.go`. The `Service` struct (ProvideService) manages the complete lifecycle of backend plugins:\\n\\n- **Start method**: Initiates plugin processes for managed backend plugins and launches automatic crash recovery via `startPluginAndKeepItAlive`\\n- **keepPluginAlive function**: Implements the restart policy by continuously monitoring plugin processes using a ticker (default 1-second intervals). When a plugin crashes (detected via `p.Exited()`), it automatically restarts the process using `p.Start(context.Background())`\\n- **Stop method**: Gracefully terminates plugin processes by calling `p.Decommission()` and `p.Stop(ctx)`\\n\\nThe `Manager` interface in `pkg/plugins/manager/process/ifaces.go` defines the contract with Start and Stop methods.\\n\\n## gRPC Client Connection\\n\\ngRPC communication to backend plugins is handled through multiple coordinated components:\\n\\n**grpc_plugin.go**: The `grpcPlugin` struct implements the `backendplugin.Plugin` interface:\\n- Uses `hashicorp/go-plugin` with gRPC protocol version negotiation\\n- Maintains connection state with pluginState enum (NotStarted, StartInit, StartSuccess, StartFail, Stopped)\\n- The `Start` method creates a new plugin.Client and negotiates protocol version\\n- The `Stop` method kills the client process via `p.client.Kill()`\\n- The `getPluginClient` method checks if the client is alive and ready\\n\\n**client.go**: Provides factory functions and configuration:\\n- `NewBackendPlugin` creates managed plugin factories\\n- `newClientConfig` builds go-plugin ClientConfig with gRPC handshake, versioned plugins, and environment variables\\n- Supports both process mode and container mode execution\\n- Integrates OpenTelemetry tracing via `otelgrpc.NewClientHandler`\\n\\n**client_v2.go**: The `ClientV2` struct aggregates gRPC service clients:\\n- Combines DiagnosticsClient, ResourceClient, DataClient, StreamClient, AdmissionClient, ConversionClient, and RendererPlugin\\n- `newClientV2` dispenses and wraps individual gRPC clients from the plugin connection\\n\\n**client_proto.go**: The `ProtoClient` interface provides the high-level gRPC client abstraction:\\n- Wraps the internal `grpcPlugin` for external consumption\\n- Methods like QueryData, CallResource, CheckHealth delegate to underlying ClientV2 implementations\\n\\n## Health Check Implementation\\n\\nHealth checking is integrated throughout the gRPC layer:\\n\\n- **grpcPlugin.CheckHealth**: Routes health check requests through `getPluginClient` to ensure plugin availability\\n- **ClientV2.CheckHealth**: Implements the actual gRPC health check call to the plugin's DiagnosticsClient\\n  - Handles Unimplemented status gracefully (returns HealthStatusUnknown)\\n  - Converts between backend.CheckHealthRequest and pluginv2 protobuf messages\\n  - Returns error if plugin client is unavailable\\n\\n## Plugin Restart Policy on Crash\\n\\nThe crash recovery system is sophisticated:\\n\\n1. **Automatic Detection**: `keepPluginAlive` continuously polls via ticker, detecting crashed processes through `p.Exited()`\\n2. **Non-Core Plugin Only**: Core plugins are excluded from restart monitoring (checked in `startPluginAndKeepItAlive`)\\n3. **Graceful Restart**: On crash detection, the system logs the event and attempts restart via `p.Start(context.Background())`\\n4. **Error Handling**: If restart fails, the error is logged but the monitoring continues trying in future ticks\\n5. **Graceful Shutdown**: Decommissioned plugins are detected and monitoring stops automatically\\n\\n## Initialization and Termination Pipeline\\n\\n**initialization/steps.go**: \\n- `BackendClientInit.Initialize`: Registers backend plugin clients using `BackendFactoryProvider`\\n- `BackendClientStarter.Start`: Invokes the process manager to start the backend plugin process\\n\\n**termination/steps.go**:\\n- `BackendProcessTerminator.Terminate`: Delegates to process.Manager.Stop for clean shutdown\\n- `Deregister.Deregister`: Removes plugins from the registry after termination\\n\\nThe backend plugin system in Grafana provides resilient, self-healing plugin process management with automatic crash recovery, gRPC-based inter-process communication, and integrated health checking.\"\n}\n",
